ATM	472	MSKCC	GRCh37	11	108203575	108203576	+	missense_variant	Missense_Mutation	DNP	TG	TG	GC	rs267606668		P-0046695-T01-IM6									Unknown	GERMLINE				MSK-IMPACT			124	105			ENST00000278616.4:c.7875_7876delinsGC	p.Asp2625_Ala2626delinsGluPro	p.D2625_A2626delinsEP	ENST00000278616	NM_000051.3	2625	gaTGct/gaGCct	53/63														This heterozygous variant c.7875_7876delTGinsGC results in the substitution of two amino acids in the ATM protein (p.Asp2625_Ala2626delinsGluPro). This variant is absent from large population databases (1000 Genomes, ESP, and gnomAD), and has been reported in both the compound heterozygous and homozygous states in multiple families with ataxia telangiectasia (PMID: 9521587, 10980530, 19535770). In an experimental study, this variant led to impaired kinase activity of ATM protein (PMID: 22213089, 30549301).  In summary, based on the previous reports of this variant in individuals with ATM associated disease and functional studies showing a loss of ATM protein function, this variant is classified as likely pathogenic.  Note: this variant may also be referred to as a double missense change D2625E and A2626P in the literature  ATM truncating mutations may increase the risk of breast cancer and pancreatic cancer (PMID: 21787400; PMID: 22585167) and have been reported in families with familial prostate cancer (PMID: 24556621.)   Ataxia-telangiectasia is an autosomal recessive condition characterized by progressive cerebellar ataxia,   telangiectasias, immunodeficiency, and increased cancer risks and is caused by two mutations (one affecting each allele) in the ATM gene.  If an ATM mutation carrier's partner is heterozygous for a pathogenic ATM mutation, there is a 25% risk that each child would be affected by ataxia-telangiectasia.																												0																																								SUCCESS
APC	324	MSKCC	GRCh37	5	112175211	112175211	+	missense_variant	Missense_Mutation	SNP	T	T	A	rs1801155		P-0065645-T01-IM7									Unknown	GERMLINE				MSK-IMPACT			187	86			ENST00000257430.4:c.3920T>A	p.Ile1307Lys	p.I1307K	ENST00000257430	NM_000038.5	1307	aTa/aAa	16/16														The APC c.3920T>A variant changes an Isoleucine at codon 1307 to a Lysine (p.Ile1307Lys). This variant has been found in 6-10% of the Ashkenazi Jewish population (PMID:9288102 , 23896379.) A large meta analysis found that Ashkenazi Jews carrying the p.Ile1307Lys variant had approximately a 2-fold increased risk of colorectal cancer (OR=2.17, 95% CI=1.65-2.86). However, this same study did not find any increased risk of colorectal cancer among non-Ashkenazi Jews who carry this variant (OR=1.36, 95% CI=0.59-3.13) (PMID: 23576677). In summary, this is a common sequence change that is associated with a 2-fold increased risk of colorectal cancer in the Ashkenazi Jewish population.																												0																																								SUCCESS

Computational prediction tools (SIFT, PolyPhen2, and MutationTaster) suggest that this variant may impact to the protein.  This variant is classified as pathogenic. Lynch syndrome is an autosomal dominant condition that confers an increased risk for colorectal cancer and endometrial cancers as well as other cancers.  There is a 50% chance that each child would inherit this variant from a carrier parent.																												0																																								SUCCESS

This heterozygous FANCC c.456+4A>T germline variant occurs in the 5' splice consensus sequence in intron 5 of the FANCC gene. It has been reported in many homozygous patients with Fanconi anemia (PubMed 8348157, 8081385, 10666230), and is a considered a founder mutation in the Ashkenazi Jewish population (detected in 0.6% of Ashkenazi Jewish chromosomes by the Genome Aggregation Database (gnomAD : http://gnomad.broadinstitute.org  )). Experimental studies have shown that this variant disrupts splicing (PubMed 8348157). In summary, based on the biallelic occurrence of this variant in individuals with Fanconi anemia, this variant meets our criteria to be classified as pathogenic for autosomal recessive Fanconi anemia. Fanconi anemia (FA) is an autosomal recessive disorder that can be caused by biallelic variants in FANCC, and is characterized by physical abnormalities, bone marrow failure, and increased risk for malignancy (https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/books/NBK1401/).																												0																																								SUCCESS
APC	324	MSKCC	GRCh37	5	112175211	112175211	+	missense_variant	Missense_Mutation	SNP	T	T	A	rs1801155		P-0047449-T01-IM6									Unknown	GERMLINE				MSK-IMPACT			105	109			ENST00000257430.4:c.3920T>A	p.Ile1307Lys	p.I1307K	ENST00000257430	NM_000038.5	1307	aTa/aAa	16/16														The APC c.3920T>A variant changes an Isoleucine at codon 1307 to a Lysine (p.Ile1307Lys). This variant has been found in 6-10% of the Ashkenazi Jewish population (PMID:9288102 , 23896379.) A large meta analysis found that Ashkenazi Jews carrying the p.Ile1307Lys variant had approximately a 2-fold increased risk of colorectal cancer (OR=2.17, 95% CI=1.65-2.86). However, this same study did not find any increased risk of colorectal cancer among non-Ashkenazi Jews who carry this variant (OR=1.36, 95% CI=0.59-3.13) (PMID: 23576677). This variant has been found in 6-10% of the Ashkenazi Jewish population (PMID:9288102 , 23896379.) A large meta analysis found that Ashkenazi Jews carrying the p.Ile1307Lys variant had approximately a 2-fold increased risk of colorectal cancer (OR=2.17, 95% CI=1.65-2.86). Truncating variants in PMS2 are known to be pathogenic. This variant has been identified in 0.002% chromosomes by the Genome Aggregation Database (gnomAD : http://gnomad.broadinstitute.org).  It has been reported in the literature in individuals with colon cancer and Lynch syndrome, with several tumors showing an MSI-H phenotype and/or isolated loss of PMS2 on immunostaining (PMID: 20205264, 23709753, 22918162, 27589204).  It has been classified by the International Society for Gastrointestinal Hereditary Tumours as pathogenic (http://insight-group.org/).  In summary, based on the previous reports of this variant in individuals with PMS2 associated cancers and its truncating effect on the protein, this variant is classified as pathogenic.   Lynch syndrome is an autosomal dominant condition that confers an increased risk for colorectal cancer and endometrial cancers as well as other cancers.
